This is consistent\n * with Zookeeper Digest-MD5 implementation.\n * <p>\n * To avoid storing clear passwords on disk or to integrate with external authentication\n * servers in production systems, this module can be replaced with a different implementation.\n *\n */\npublic class PlainSaslServer implements SaslServer {\n\n    public static final String PLAIN_MECHANISM = \"PLAIN\";\n\n    private final CallbackHandler callbackHandler;\n    private boolean complete;\n    private String authorizationId;\n\n    public PlainSaslServer(CallbackHandler callbackHandler) {\n        this.callbackHandler = callbackHandler;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * @throws SaslAuthenticationException if username/password combination is invalid or if the requested\n     *         authorization id is not the same as username.\n     * <p>\n     * <b>Note:</b> This method may throw {@link SaslAuthenticationException} to provide custom error messages\n     * to clients. instanceof SslAuthenticationContext) {\n            SSLSession sslSession = ((SslAuthenticationContext) context).session();\n            try {\n                return (context instanceof SaslAuthenticationContext) {\n            SaslServer saslServer = ((SaslAuthenticationContext) context).server();\n            if authentication implementation is centered on several key components:\\n\\n1. **SASL Server Authenticator Core**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java` implements the `Authenticator` interface and manages the authentication lifecycle. It maintains state through an enum `SaslState` and handles the SASL handshake request parsing and mechanism selection.\\n\\n2. **Mechanism Selection**: In `SaslServerAuthenticator.handleHandshakeRequest()`, the broker receives the client's requested SASL mechanism and validates it against the list of enabled mechanisms. If the mechanism is supported, it creates the appropriate SASL server via `createSaslServer()`. For GSSAPI/Kerberos, it uses `createSaslKerberosServer()` which extracts service principal information from the server's JAAS-authenticated subject.\\n\\n3. **Mechanism-Specific Implementations**:\\n   - **PLAIN**: `PlainSaslServer.java` with inner class `PlainSaslServerFactory` implements RFC 4616 username/password authentication\\n   - **SCRAM**: `ScramSaslServer.java` with inner class `ScramSaslServerFactory` implements RFC 5802 SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512\\n   - **OAUTHBEARER**: `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java` with inner class `OAuthBearerSaslServerFactory` implements OAuth 2.0 Bearer Token authentication\\n   - **GSSAPI**: Standard Java SASL with Kerberos (created via `Sasl.createSaslServer()` call in `SaslServerAuthenticator`)\\n\\n4. **Mechanism Providers**: Each mechanism has a corresponding provider that registers with Java's Security API:\\n   - `PlainSaslServerProvider.java` registers `PlainSaslServerFactory`\\n   - `ScramSaslServerProvider.java` registers `ScramSaslServerFactory` for both SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512\\n   - `OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider.java` registers `OAuthBearerSaslServerFactory`\\n\\n5. **Authentication Context Lifecycle**: `SaslAuthenticationContext.java` represents the authentication context containing the `SaslServer`, security protocol, client address, and optional SSL session information. This is created during authentication and passed to the principal builder.\\n\\n6. **Callback Handlers**: Mechanism-specific callback handlers implement credential validation:\\n   - `PlainServerCallbackHandler.java` validates username/password from JAAS configuration\\n   - `ScramServerCallbackHandler.java` retrieves SCRAM credentials and delegation tokens from credential caches\\n   - `SaslServerCallbackHandler.java` handles default callbacks including realm and authorization for GSSAPI\\n\\n7. **Server Setup**: `SaslChannelBuilder.java` is responsible for setting up SASL on the broker side. In `createServerCallbackHandlers()`, it instantiates the appropriate callback handler for each enabled mechanism. In `buildServerAuthenticator()`, it creates the `SaslServerAuthenticator` instance with all necessary configuration, subjects, and callback handlers.\\n\\n8. **Login Modules**: Each mechanism has a login module that initializes the corresponding SASL provider at class load time:\\n   - `PlainLoginModule.java` initializes `PlainSaslServerProvider`\\n   - `ScramLoginModule.java` initializes both `ScramSaslClientProvider` and `ScramSaslServerProvider`\\n   - `OAuthBearerLoginModule.java` initializes both providers\\n\\n9. **Mechanism Constants**: `ScramMechanism.java` defines the SCRAM mechanism variants (SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512) with their hash algorithms and iteration counts.\\n\\n10. **Principal Building**: `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java` uses `SaslAuthenticationContext` to extract the authenticated principal.
